Meeting of the Zhabei Defense Corps

▲ The First, Second, Seventh, and Eighth Squads Have Already Been Deployed for Defense ▲ Planning to Investigate, Register, Organize, and Consolidate. Wang Binyan, the head of the Zhabei Defense Corps, after our side took over the Fourth District Headquarters and the First and Second Sub-Offices, convened a temporary emergency corps affairs meeting at the Zhabei Corps Headquarters yesterday afternoon at 2:00 PM to restore the Defense Corps. The various circumstances are recorded below:

▲ The Corps Affairs Meeting was attended by Corps Head Wang Binyan, Special Affairs Director Jiang Huaishu, Special Affairs Deputy Director Feng Yixian, Squad Leader of the First Squad Yu Xipin, Squad Leader of the Second Squad Xu Youtang, Squad Leader of the Third Squad Mo Meiqing, Squad Leader of the Fourth Squad Na Minyi, Squad Leader of the Fifth Squad Liu Changqi, Squad Leader of the Sixth Squad Hou Yuncai, Squad Leader of the Seventh Squad Chen Yuxin, Squad Leader of the Eighth Squad Lu Lilang, Squad Leader of the Ninth Reserve Squad Wang Delin, and Guard Squad Leader Li Xiuling. Wang Binyan presided over the meeting, and Li Xiuling recorded the minutes. First, the chairman reported on the assistance provided to the military and police during the war. Then, discussions began on (1) Corps Head Wang's proposal on how to restore the local Defense Corps. It was resolved to proceed with consolidation as soon as possible to facilitate restoration. (2) Special Affairs Director Jiang's proposal to actively investigate the original members of each squad and register any deaths and losses of firearms. The proposal was passed. (3) Squad Leader She's proposal to negotiate the dismantling and opening of the barbed wire on the Xinzhapu Bridge to facilitate traffic. The proposal was passed. (4) Squad Leader Mo's proposal that it is difficult to investigate corps members because some Japanese troops have not completely withdrawn. It was resolved to find ways to investigate. (5) The areas of the Third, Fourth, Fifth, and Sixth Squads are difficult to restore because the Japanese troops have not withdrawn. It was resolved to start work. (6) Regarding the large number of firearms lost or privately hidden in the areas of the Seventh and Eighth Squads, how should they be handled? It was resolved that the squad leaders should find ways to collect them or purchase them with funds, and report to the corps headquarters beforehand. (7) The Beiping police are not familiar with the local situation and urgently need assistance to maintain order. The proposal was passed. (8) A letter from the flour industry stated that a lot of wheat flour being transported in the Suzhou River is being stolen, and they request defense to maintain commercial goods. It was resolved that the Ninth Squad should be deployed for defense.

▲ Restoration Plan. A reporter from the New Voice Press met Corps Head Wang Binyan yesterday and asked about the plan to restore the Zhabei Defense Corps. According to him, the Zhabei Defense Corps has eight squads, each with 100 members, six corps soldiers, one squad leader, three platoon leaders, and one clerk, totaling 112 people, as well as the Guard Squad, the Ninth Reserve Squad (i.e., the Water Patrol Squad). The total number is more than 1,000 people. When the Shanghai Incident occurred, they assisted the military and police in maintaining local order. After our army retreated, they followed to places such as Qingpu and Suzhou, and most of the firearms were transported out, so fortunately, there were few losses. However, the exercise of duties had to be temporarily suspended. Now that our side has taken over the jurisdiction of the four districts of Zhabei, we will immediately find ways to restore it. As for the restoration plan, the first step is to report the deployment, the second step is to investigate, the third step is to register, and the fourth step is to organize and consolidate. The previous regular expenses were 1,434 yuan per month, which was allocated by the municipal government. It was stopped after the Shanghai Incident. Now it has been decided to request temporary expenses from the municipal government, which should not be a problem. Starting yesterday, the members of the First Squad, Second Squad, Seventh Squad, Eighth Squad, and Ninth Reserve Squad in Shanghai have been deployed for defense. However, the Third Squad, Fourth Squad, Fifth Squad, and Sixth Squad have not been deployed because the Japanese troops have not withdrawn from their areas, but they have already reported for duty and will be restored after the withdrawal.

Sending Refugees Back Home

The Jia Ding Fellow Villagers Association on Avenue Joffre, in view of the fact that the Japanese troops in the county have withdrawn one after another and order has been restored as usual, has specially prepared many ships to send the fellow villagers who have taken refuge in Shanghai back home. The ships are under the Xinyang Bridge. The departure time depends on the tides. Those who want to take the ship can register with the association first so that they can be sent to the dock.

The Flower and Yarn Industry Volunteer Army Returns from the Front Lines

The Flower and Yarn Industry Volunteer Army of this city, after the January 28th Incident, was deployed to Pudong and was responsible for the transportation of supplies for the Shanghai Garrison. Later, they were ordered to be reorganized into the Protection Unit of the Transportation Department of the 19th Route Army, stationed in places such as Su Kun for work. It has been two months now, and with the situation coming to an end, they urgently need to be withdrawn for rest. Therefore, the district captain Lu Junlin led them back to Shanghai. They arrived in Shanghai at 8:00 AM yesterday. Due to other reasons, they changed their landing point to Pu Zuo. More than 100 people, including representatives of the Yarn Industry Association, the Cotton Industry Federation, the Women's Comfort Association, and local defense corps, went to the port to welcome them. The team members have been away from their hometowns for a long time and have endured hardships. One day, they returned to their hometowns, and they were all in high spirits. Then, Chen Zixin, the administrative committee member and defense corps leader of Yangsi Township, hosted a banquet. During the banquet, Chen delivered a welcoming speech, and squadron leader Yang Xixian expressed his gratitude and reported on the details of participating in the battle of the 19th Route Army. It is said that the army has been praised by the superiors for its past achievements and has received many firearms, military flags, commemorative medals, and awards, which are very precious.

Report on the Tragic Spring Famine in Jiangsu

Cheng Jingsheng stated that the National Government Relief Association allocated 80,000 yuan to Jiangsu for spring relief, which was not enough to provide relief, so the association's Chairman Song telegraphed: To Chairman Song and Vice Chairman Xin of the National Government Disaster Relief Committee, and Director Zhu of the Work Group, I acknowledge receipt of the Director's telegram allocating 80,000 yuan to Jiangsu to relieve the spring famine in the counties north of the Yangtze River. At this time of national difficulty, it is a great act to relieve the disaster-stricken people, and all who are aware cannot help but shed tears of gratitude. However, after investigating the counties north of the Yangtze River, the disaster is too heavy, and the spring famine is worse than the winter famine. Although winter relief has been implemented, if spring relief is not continued, deaths will follow one another at the time of the green and yellow unripened crops. This can be predicted early. Therefore, Jingsheng submitted a request in a supporting telegram in February of this year, which was not only listed as the reason for Jingsheng's resignation, but also predicted the situation that the spring relief would not be done and the previous efforts would be abandoned, as well as the situation that various groups would be unable to continue the relief. Later, on the Geng Day, Shan Day, Xin Day, and You Day in February, continuous telegrams were sent requesting at least 500,000 yuan for spring relief to select the most affected areas for relief. On Zheng Day in March, the methods for sending spring relief were resubmitted. At that time, the war was not over, and the association had difficulty raising funds and violated the reply telegram. Resignation was not allowed, but the increase in funds was beyond reach. The environment made it impossible to do anything but sigh. Recently, what Jingsheng predicted has unfortunately become a reality one by one. Therefore, there were requests again on Jing Day in April, Qin Day, and Dong Day of this month. The current state of misery and the cessation of life chances cannot be remedied by a small amount of relief funds. I would like to respectfully report to you separately (1) The current situation of the disaster victims in various counties cutting off food. In Xinghua, Gaoyou, and other counties, the winter relief has been exhausted, and there is no hope for spring wheat. They are digging and eating the mineral white soil (commonly known as Guanyin powder), which causes intestinal astringency and difficulty in bowel movements, and many people have died. In Dongtai, Yancheng, Fuyang, Shaobo, Baoying, Taixian, and other places, there is also little spring wheat. They eat perennial animals. After the aquatic products are exhausted, they continue to eat artemisia and other wild plants, and their faces are swollen. Those who die are gray in color and look like they have been poisoned. Moreover, gatherings of people to cause disturbances occur several times a day. Those who commit suicide by jumping into the river are often heard. In Huaiyin, Siyang, Huai'an, Tongshan, Xiaoxian, Pixian, Suqian, Yangzhou, Lianshui, Jiangpu, and Liuhe, the land is originally full of springs, and although wheat is planted, they cannot wait for it to ripen. They often use green seedlings to fill their stomachs, cutting off their own livelihood. The situation is very pitiful. According to reports, in the fourth district of Pixian County, more than 110 people starved to death on Dong Day of this month. In Xiaoxian County, there is a family that has committed suicide in a row, thousands and tens of thousands of people are running around and shouting, swimming and arriving, taking risks, and it is impossible to prevent them. The above situation is not only the case in four counties. In the cities, there are also many people who are cut off and waiting to die. (2) The reason why the amount of money is not enough for relief. The amount of money and goods from the winter and urgent relief, combined with the implementation of various groups, is about more than 3.6 million yuan, and there is still a shortage at times. Spring relief has always been considered to have more households than winter relief. In addition, after the war, not only those who used to live in the south of the Yangtze River and support themselves have returned one after another, but also those who have lived in Songhu for a long time and live by working have also returned to the north of the Yangtze River with the elderly and children, adding tens of thousands of unemployed people every day, adding to the number of people waiting for relief. Roughly speaking, those who cannot live without relief total more than 3 million people. If we talk about the situation, even if there are more than 3.6 million, the amount is still huge. Moreover, the groups have no money to help, and the 80,000 yuan issued by the association is only 1% or 2% of the urgent winter relief. If it is said to be strict elimination, it is actually impossible to eliminate. If it is said to be strict investigation, it is also impossible to investigate. Not only is it difficult to provide great relief, but it is also impossible to start. (3) The plan to select the best for relief. Since the association's relief funds are already very difficult, I dare to ask for 500,000 yuan to start with the above 19 counties. The severely affected counties can get 45,000 yuan, and the less severely affected counties can get 12,000 yuan. Depending on the local situation, either set up porridge factories, or still check households to give leaders, or still subsidize the incomplete embankment projects. Each county will first implement the most severe areas in the severely affected areas, and then ask various charities to raise funds to promote and cooperate in order to reduce deaths slightly, so that the desire for kindness can be achieved, and people can be saved completely, but only to delay death for a moment, to appease and appease, but to stop the chaos from sprouting slightly. If you are willing to approve, I will respectfully submit the grades of severity of the various counties separately, as well as the cooperation methods with the charities, for review and approval to see if they are appropriate. Respectfully awaiting your decision. Cheng Jingsheng, Commissioner of Jiangsu, Koutou, Han.

Gao Youtang Replies to the Letter from the Anti-Drug Association

Gao Youtang, a member of the Supervisory Yuan, replied to the letter from the Anti-Drug Association yesterday, stating: To the Chinese National Anti-Drug Association, I acknowledge receipt of your letter while traveling in Los Angeles. It is an honor to receive your award, and I am deeply grateful. The impeachment of Liu Ruiheng was proposed in the fall of last year, but the government put it aside and did not deal with it. Recently, the Disciplinary Committee was established, and the Executive Yuan transferred it to the committee. Whether to punish him or not is the right of the committee. Currently, open cultivation, transportation, sale, and smoking are rampant in Hunan, Hubei, Anhui, and Kaifeng, and it is heard that Hebei, Shanxi, Rehe, Chahar, and Suiyuan are also thinking of following suit, raising funds in name, but in fact enriching themselves. My colleagues are collecting evidence and plan to impeach them one by one to fulfill their responsibilities. Whether the government can handle it according to law is difficult to predict. For me, I am only making the listeners aware of the warning. In the future, if your association obtains evidence, I hope you will teach me at any time, and I will be very welcome. I have received the papers in the monthly journal that you sent, and I have read them with admiration. I would like to express my thanks and wish you all the best. Gao Youtang, Qiqi.

There are Four Articles in the Company Law Enforcement Act That Extend the Implementation Period

The Municipal Social Affairs Bureau received an order from the Ministry of Industry, stating that Article 11 of the Company Law Enforcement Act stipulates that stocks and bonds of limited companies that have not been signed and sealed by five or more directors should be signed and sealed by five or more current directors within one year after the implementation of the Company Law. Also, according to Article 6 of the same law, if the stock payment paid before the implementation of the Company Law is less than one-half of the par value of the stock, the insufficient part should be paid up in accordance with the law within one year after the implementation of the Company Law. According to Article 12, if a company issues bearer shares exceeding one-third of the total number of shares before the implementation of the Company Law, the excess number of shares should be changed to registered shares within one year of the implementation of the Company Law. According to Article 13, if the shares issued by a company before the implementation of the Company Law do not comply with the second provision of Article 115 of the Company Law, they should be corrected in accordance with the law within one year after the implementation of the Company Law. The amendment period for the aforementioned provisions will expire on June 30 of this year. Although many companies have followed and reported the corrections, there are also many who have not followed due to various difficulties. In order to understand the difficulties of businesses and to ensure that all companies comply with the new law, the Ministry has submitted to the Executive Yuan and then to the National Government for approval to extend the period by one year (i.e., extend the period to June 30, 1933). The bureau has ordered the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce to notify all companies to follow the instructions.

Shanghai Customs of Out-of-Stock Stores

▲ The Municipal Chamber of Commerce Replied to Lawyer Zhou Xiao's Letter. The sale of a store is prone to disputes. According to Article 21 of the Merchant's General Rules, the transfer of a business name shall not be used to oppose a third party unless it is a transfer of registration. The legal provisions are very clear. Recently, a large merchant was involved in a lawsuit over the sale of a store, and Lawyer Zhou Xiao'an was handling the case. However, what are the customs of Shanghai merchants in this regard? We have sent a letter to the Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce to inquire. The reply from the chamber is recorded below. (Dear Sir, I have received your letter, inquiring whether it is necessary to register the sale of a store according to Shanghai merchant customs after the sale, and whether this registration system is implemented in this city. We have sent personnel to investigate. The current situation in this city is that whether a store is registered or not depends on whether the store was registered with the Ministry of Industry before the sale. If it was registered before, it should still be registered after the sale so that a new certificate can be exchanged and the registered benefits can be continued. Otherwise, no registration procedures have been handled. If the store was registered with the Municipal Social Affairs Bureau for industry and commerce before the sale, it must also apply for registration with the Social Affairs Bureau after the sale and issue a business license to the purchaser. Otherwise, there is no need to go through the registration procedures. This is the case for general stores. As for whether the registration system is implemented in this city, the Ministry of Industry handles the registration of companies and businesses in order to understand the organization, capital, and business of the businesses and to protect all the legal interests of the businesses. There are no regulations that force businesses to register, so its authority is limited to those who have been registered. If they have not been registered, they are generally not consulted. Therefore, according to the current situation, the registration system and registration procedures have not been widely implemented. We hereby reply to you by letter, and please check. Shanghai Municipal Chamber of Commerce)

Song Zigao Entices and Murders Fellow Villager

▲ Previously Committed Murder and Escaped to Shanghai ▲ Sun Baohua Extorted Money and Was Killed Song Zigao, also known as Li Xingting, a native of Songjiang, worked as an inspector at the Kungsheng Yuan in the Nine Acres area. On the evening of the 24th of last month, he lured his fellow villager Sun Baohua, who resided at No. 84 Xujiahui Road in the French Concession, to the Great World entertainment complex. He suddenly produced a bayonet and attempted to kill Sun, stabbing him in the neck. He then placed a forged suicide note in Sun's pocket and fled. The Great World reported the incident to the police, who sent Sun to Renji Hospital for treatment. Meanwhile, Su Deshan, a detective from the special agency of the French police, discovered that Song was hiding in Room 24 of the Jiangxin Hotel in the Zhoujin Lane on the Fourth Road. On the 27th of the same month, they went to arrest him, but Song resisted arrest, causing Su's chest to be injured. He was eventually apprehended and taken back to the police station, then escorted to the Second Special Court for interrogation and investigation. The police have now learned that at the end of 1919, Song and Shen Aqin murdered a widowed woman surnamed Zhang and two others near the Xiuye Bridge outside the West Gate of Songjiang. After the incident, Shen was arrested and executed, while Song escaped to Anhui. In the spring of 1930, he came to Shanghai and worked at Kungsheng Yuan. Sun found out about this and frequently extorted money from Song, leading Song to harbor resentment and plot to kill Sun. On March 3rd, March 16th, and April 19th, he tricked Sun into writing a will under false pretenses and secretly stamped it with Sun's seal. Finally, on April 24th, he lured Sun to the Great World and carried out the murder, stabbing Sun in the neck with a bayonet and stuffing the forged will into Sun's pocket before fleeing. The police prepared a detailed report and are prosecuting him for premeditated attempted murder under Articles 284, Sections 1 and 3 of the Criminal Code. Yesterday at 11:00 AM, Judge Xiong Huiping from the Third Criminal Court continued the hearing. First, the police lawyer Fei Xizhen presented the case, requesting that the law be applied. The victim, Sun Baohua, who had recovered from his injuries and been discharged from the hospital, also appeared in court to testify about the circumstances of the attempted murder. When questioned, Song Zigao admitted to attempting to murder Sun Baohua and resisting arrest. He evaded the question regarding the murder case in Songjiang. The court reviewed the evidence and adjourned the hearing to a later date. The defendant was returned to custody. The Cao Qingcheng Assassination Case

Dog Secures Two Murderers

▲ Gun Found in Murderers' Room ▲ Defendant Claims Tao Guanzheng Masterminded the Assassination Cao Qingcheng, a native of Hubei who resided at No. 41 Yuansheng Lane, Route Lafayette in the French Concession and worked as an inspector at the Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau, was shot and killed by assassins in front of No. 184 Carler Road at 1:30 PM the day before yesterday. Two bullets struck his head, killing him instantly. At the same time, the assassins mistakenly wounded Jin Shoupei, a native of Jiangwan who lived at No. 25 in the same lane as Cao, in the abdomen and back. Detectives pursued and apprehended two of the murderers, seizing a handgun and twenty-one bullets from each. They were taken to the police station. Jin was sent to Guangci Hospital for treatment, and Cao's body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan funeral parlor for an autopsy. Details of the case were reported in yesterday's newspaper. It has now been learned that during the night, the captured criminals were interrogated by the police chief. One, named Liu Guobao, 17 years old, from Sichuan, residing at No. 305 Weihaiwei Road, and the other, named Li Shiying, 22 years old, from Henan, with no fixed address, both confessed that Tao Guanzheng, who is still at large, masterminded the assassination. They stated that Tao resided at the Yanzhi (cigarette paper) store at No. 980 Huade Road in the Public Concession. The special agency immediately dispatched Chinese and Western detectives, together with Chinese and Western police officers from the Public Concession, to Tao's residence at No. 980 Huade Road. They seized two handguns, two pairs of handcuffs, two daggers, a saw, and acid, among other items. They also took the second landlord, Zhu Jinming, a native of Hangzhou, into custody. The following morning, Li Zecai, a native of Anhui, was apprehended at No. 305 Weihaiwei Road and brought to the police station. Because Tao had privately stockpiled weapons, and there was concern that he may have committed other crimes, the Public Concession Police sent the two handguns to the French Police for examination to determine if they had been used in any other crimes. Yesterday at 10:00 AM, the Criminal Division of the French Police requested that the Second Special Court appoint Prosecutor Wu Xiaoke, accompanied by a forensic doctor, to examine the body and conduct an inquest. The presiding judge heard a report from the police chief and then heard a statement from Cao's widow, Mrs. Cao Hu, who said that her husband had gone out to buy a raincoat the day before and was tragically murdered. She sought justice. The official autopsy determined that Cao Qingcheng had died from gunshot wounds to the head sustained before death. The widow took custody of the body for burial. The arrested criminals will be sent to court for questioning. Subsequently, at 11:00 AM, the police escorted the four criminals to the Second Special Court, where Presiding Judge Wang Gangxu, along with Prosecutor Wu and Clerk Zhu Chengzhuo, conducted a preliminary hearing in the First Criminal Court. Gu Shouxi, the police lawyer, presented the case, stating that the police were temporarily prosecuting the defendants for premeditated murder under Articles 282 and 284, Section 1, of the Criminal Code. However, due to time constraints, the police had not yet completed their investigation and requested that the court adjourn the hearing for two weeks to allow for further investigation. The handguns, bullets, and other items were presented as evidence. Presiding Judge Wang briefly questioned the defendants. Liu and Li both confessed that Tao Guanzheng, who is still at large, had instructed them to carry out the assassination the day before. Zhu and Li both claimed to have no knowledge of the assassination. The court adjourned the hearing until May 31st, and the defendants were temporarily remanded to police custody. Yang Jingcun, a native of Anhui

Accused of Abandonment and Assault

▲ Defendant is the Nephew of the Late Military Governor ▲ Aunt Mrs. Yang Zhang Also Accused ▲ Plaintiff is a Former Courtesan and Yang's Concubine ▲ Demands Punishment, Compensation, and Divorce Yang Jingcun, a native of Anhui and nephew of the late Zhejiang Military Governor Yang Shande, and his aunt, Mrs. Yang Zhang, have recently been sued by Kong Chen, a 45-year-old woman from Zhenjiang residing at No. 2006 Fukang Lane, Hai'ning Road, North Zhejiang Road, along with her daughter Yang Kong, also known as Shujun, 24 years old. They have retained lawyer Zhao Zuwei to file a complaint with the First Special District Court, accusing them of mistreatment, abandonment, and joint assault, along with a civil lawsuit. The facts of the complaint are as follows: the plaintiffs are a mother and daughter. Shujun initially worked as a courtesan, and the defendant Yang Jingcun often visited. Knowing that Shujun had some savings, he repeatedly enticed her, and they married in the first month of the lunar calendar two years ago. No bride price was paid, and no written contract was made. Initially, their love was strong, but over time, Yang grew tired of her. Because Shujun was physically weak and unwilling to prepare his opium pipes late into the night, he gradually saw her as a thorn in his side. Mrs. Yang Zhang, Jingcun's aunt, acted as his accomplice, constantly scolding and beating her, treating her like an enemy. The houses at No. 2006 to No. 2008 Fukang Lane are all owned by Jingcun. Shujun had deposited 300 yuan in her own name at the Four Banks Savings Society in June of the previous year and another 100 yuan in July, which were subsequently taken by Yang. When they moved into Fukang Lane, Yang refused to provide any household items, so Shujun used her own money to buy furniture and other items for their use. For the past two years, he has not provided any living expenses, which Shujun has covered with her own savings, spending over 1,000 yuan on household expenses. Now that her savings are depleted, the defendant not only shows no remorse but has intensified his abuse, constantly scolding and beating her. Her situation is so dire that she fears she will soon die. Even more unexpectedly, during the recent war, the plaintiff Kong Chen and her son Fan Kun came to Shanghai to seek refuge and temporarily lived with Shujun. On April 8th, for unknown reasons, the two defendants became angry and began scolding them from No. 2008 to No. 2006, and physically assaulted the mother and son. At the time, fearing their ferocity, they dared not retaliate. On the 18th, they again assaulted Kun in the lane. Kong Chen heard the commotion and went to investigate and was also beaten, causing her to bleed profusely. They called the police, who took her to a hospital for treatment and initiated a lawsuit. However, the police believed it was a domestic dispute and refused to represent them, leaving them with no recourse. The two defendants are guilty of assault under Article 293 of the Criminal Code and abandonment under Article 310 of the same code and should be severely punished according to the law. The defendants' actions are cruel and have completely severed any sense of obligation. It is impossible for Shujun to continue living with them, so she requests permission to sever her family ties with the defendant Mrs. Yang Zhang and requests that both defendants jointly compensate her with 200 yuan for medical expenses and 300 yuan for recuperation expenses. She also requests that Yang Jingcun return Shujun's savings of 400 yuan, the 2,200 yuan she spent on household expenses, and 20,000 yuan for alimony to support her life. The court accepted the case and issued a summons. Judge Feng Shide from the Second Criminal Court convened a hearing yesterday afternoon. Neither of the defendants appeared, nor did any lawyer represent them. The plaintiff's lawyer, Zhao Zuwei, stated that because the defendants had failed to respond to the summons, he requested that an arrest warrant be issued. Judge Feng briefly questioned the plaintiff and adjourned the case to a later date.

Two Post Office Notices

Shanghai Post Office News: The Soviet Russian airmail service between Irkutsk and Moscow, and between Moscow and various European countries, resumed on May 15th. However, this service will be suspended around November 1st of this year. Details are available on notices posted at various post offices for inquiry. It has also been learned that the Gonghe Road Postal Branch in Zhabei has resumed normal business hours from May 17th, tentatively set from 8:00 AM to 5:00 PM. However, because residents north of the Beijing-Shanghai Railway within the branch's delivery area have all relocated, mail delivery is extremely difficult. All mail will be temporarily held at the branch for collection. Recipients may contact the branch for inquiries.

The New Society (International Current Affairs) Special Issue Published

The New Society bi-monthly magazine, published at No. 150 Weihaiwei Road, Shanghai, will soon be one year old since its inception. Because many of its contributors are famous writers, it has a considerable position in the national forum. Now, it is publishing a special issue (International Current Affairs and Soviet Russia Observation). Important articles such as (Predictions on the Russian-Japanese Situation), (Current Japanese-American Relations and Predictions of Future Wars), (American War Plans Against Japan), and (The Interrelationships of China, America, Britain, and Japan) all have thorough observations on international current affairs and are excellent reference materials for those concerned with recent international events. Regarding Soviet Russia observations, there are (The Success of the Five-Year Plan and the Life of the Soviet Russian Authorities) and three translations of recent works commenting on Soviet Russia by American professor Edgar, British industrialist Owen, and British celebrity George Bernard Shaw, which can also be used for reference by those concerned with Soviet Russia. The special issue is rich in content, and its length is almost doubled compared to previous issues. Each issue is still sold for five cents, with no price increase.

Match Industry Association Approved for Industrial Organization Registration

The China National Match Industry Joint Association previously submitted its organizational outline and a list of supervisors and committee members to the former Ministry of Industry and Commerce for approval. Subsequently, the Ministry of Industry ordered that because the Joint Association was not jointly organized by match industry associations from various regions, it could instead register as an industrial organization. The association followed the regulations for registering agricultural, industrial, and mining organizations and successively submitted documents to the Shanghai Municipal Social Bureau and the Municipal Party Headquarters for approval. It then submitted the approval documents to the Ministry of Industry for review and registration. The association has now received approval from the Ministry of Industry to register as an industrial organization.

Women's Fashion Tailors Form Union Office

The women's fashion clothes and accessories currently popular in Shanghai are constantly being updated, which is very popular with women. Although there are more than 400 workers in the city, there is no organized group. Now, they are seeking to improve their business, develop production, and connect emotionally. Large Quantity of Red Pills Confiscated

▲ Involving Two Post Office Employees ▲ Thirteen-Year-Old Ningbo Child Xu Jincheng was exploited between the 11th and 13th of this month to deliver 42 packages of printed materials from the Shanghai Huishuwu Publishing House, falsely named, to the North Sichuan Road Post Office, addressed to Xuzhou. Gao, an investigator at the post office, found that they all contained a large quantity of red pills. Xu was detained, and the Hongkou Police Station dispatched Chinese Detective Shi Enjian and Western Detective Hai'er to arrest him, along with the red pills, and bring them to the police station. After questioning, they learned that the red pill operation was located at No. 66 Ximen Road in the French Concession, and the main culprit was surnamed Zhou. They secretly went and, together with French police officers, arrested four men and women surnamed Zhu and escorted them to the Second Special District Court, while Zhou fled. The Hongkou Police Station escorted Xu to the First Special Court for questioning and detention. Details have been reported in this newspaper. Subsequently, two more accomplices were apprehended: Lou Zhitian from Nanjing and Liu Desheng from Shanghai, both employees in the post office package room. Yesterday morning, they were also escorted to the First Court's Division A. Zhang Tianyin, the police lawyer, stated that the defendant Lou Zhitian was an employee of the North Sichuan Road Post Office, and Liu Desheng was employed at the Avenue Joffre Branch in the French Concession. In the adjourned hearing, Xu testified that those people had been asked to identify him. In January, those people delivered the same type of packages to Xuzhou. Those red pills, totaling 20 packages, were held up at the Nanjing Post Office due to the outbreak of war and have been telegraphed back and are now stored at the police station, for a total of 62 packages. He asked the court to question the defendants and first confiscate the red pills. When questioned, Xu testified that Liu Desheng hired a rickshaw puller to deliver the red pills to the main bureau, and Lou Zhitian checked the number of packages. The third time, because the matter had been exposed, Lou instructed me to take them back, but I was detained. I don't know what was inside. Lou Zhitian testified that a colleague surnamed Wang, who is still at large, also handled the matter and did not know that they were red pills, etc. Liu Desheng testified that he knew Xu because he had asked him to find business opportunities. Later, a colleague surnamed Chen introduced him to someone surnamed Zhou at No. 66 Ximen Road who had private printed books to send to Xuzhou. He initially refused, but later someone named Wang Lin at the main bureau agreed. Because the French Concession was strictly inspected, he asked Xu to send them to the main bureau, but [He] did not know [They] contained red pills. [Xu Jiahui Liu Desheng hired lawyer Liang Bohua, and Lou Zhitian hired lawyer Chen Ting. [Partially Obscured] Under lawyer [Partially Obscured] The Wan Huan Judge ordered all the defendants to be returned to custody, [Partially Obscured] The red pills, sixty-two packages in total, were confiscated first.

Penalties for Opium Offenders

▲ Two Women Sentenced to One Year ▲ Since the vigorous opium eradication campaign in the French Concession, a group of people who were in the business of running opium dens have found their livelihoods [Partially Obscured] Causing them to complain endlessly. They had to find other ways to make a living, so they secretly rented rooms in major hotels in the Public Concession to light lamps and provide opium for people to smoke. At around 8:00 PM the night before last, the Anti-Narcotics Department of the Public Concession Police learned that Room 415 of the Greater China Hotel on Tibet Road was being used as a secret opium den to allow people to smoke opium. Chinese Detective Song Bingzheng, Detective Zhang Shaoqing, Ding Yugao, and Western Detective Pan Gensi secretly went to the room and arrested the two people lighting the lamps, Jin Shiji and Ma Youcai, and eight opium smokers: Yang Huadi, Hu Liquan, Lu Baohua, Xi Shengbao, Ni Zhushi, Yang Xishi, and others. Along with 36 taels of opium paste, three opium lamps, two opium pipes, and one opium tray, they were taken to the Old Gate Police Station and detained separately. Yesterday morning, they were escorted to the First Criminal Court of the First Special District. Qian Xunjiu, the police lawyer, stated that Jin and Ma were prosecuted under Article 10 of the Anti-Opium Law, while the remaining defendants were prosecuted under Article 11 of the Anti-Opium Law, requesting that they be held accountable. When questioned, all the defendants denied the charges except for Jin Shiji, who admitted to selling opium. Ni Zhushi even hired lawyer Lin Yingqing to defend her. Presiding Judge Zhou Han reviewed the evidence and sentenced Jin Shiji and Ma Youcai to one year of imprisonment and a fine of 200 yuan each. Xi Shengbao was sentenced to six months of imprisonment for assisting. The remaining defendants were sentenced to one month of imprisonment each. However, the two women, Ni Zhushi and Yang Xishi, were granted a one-year suspended sentence. The opium paste and smoking paraphernalia were confiscated according to the list.

Two Suitcases of Opium

▲ Yunnan and Sichuan varieties of red and other types ▲ Total weight approximately five thousand taels of Shanghai Municipal Police Bureau 6th District 1st Precinct officers saw a small cart-puller with a cart on the Huacao road and upon questioning, discovered the heavily laden cart contained two suitcases and a bedroll. Suspecting, the officers inspected and discovered the suitcases contained Opium. The cart puller, Gu Xuegeng, said he was hired by an unknown man near Zhoujia Bridge to pull the cart to Huangdu, but did not know where to drop it off or where the man could be found near Zhoujia Bridge. He was taken into custody along with the contraband, and the evidence and cart puller were transferred to the County Court for sentencing. The Opium amounted to five to six thousand taels in weight, containing Yunnan, Sichuan, red, and other varieties.

Peace of Mind Senior Monk's Rare Birthday Celebration

Ningbo Senior Monk Peace of Mind, family name Fu, second in the family, courtesy name Yanyun, started out in the rice business. After the age of sixty, he suddenly had a great enlightenment, wore robes and became a monk, presided over the Baiyi Chan Temple in Ningbo, and served as the fundraising director for the Buddhist orphanage. He has traveled to Nanyang, the Dutch East Indies, Siam, Burma, India, and other places, raising millions of yuan each year, which he immediately remitted to local officials for orphanage education expenses to show that he was not selfish. Wearing simple robes, he visited the Four Famous Mountains. Last year, during the Shaanxi disaster, he raised a large sum of money and went to Shaanxi with General Zhu Ziqiao to provide disaster relief, saving many lives. This year, the eighteenth day of the fourth lunar month is the Senior Monk's 70th birthday. Gentlemen in Ningbo and Shanghai have each contributed cash to celebrate the Senior Monk's birthday. The money will be used to establish a farm and dormitories for the orphanage. The event is a benevolent act, and sponsors are extremely enthusiastic.

Weather Report

The Xujiahui Observatory's weather forecast at 4:30 PM yesterday stated: The Shandong coast is overcast and rainy, with winds from variable directions. The lower reaches of the Yangtze River and the coast here are overcast with heavy fog or thunderstorms, and cyclones are increasing in strength due to a low-pressure system passing through and moving eastward or northeastward. The coastal area south of Ma'an Island is cloudy, with winds from the southeast to southwest, and localized heavy fog is possible. There is a low-pressure system in the MacLiesfield Bank area. In the 24 hours before 3:00 PM yesterday, the temperature in Shanghai was a maximum of 75.7 and a minimum of 65.8. On the same day last year, the maximum was 68.7 and the minimum was 58.6.

The Opening of the Third Guiding Conference in Zhejiang Province

(Hangzhou Correspondence) The Third Guiding Conference of Zhejiang Province was held in the auditorium of the Department of Education on the morning of the 16th. In addition to Director Chen Bulei of the Department of Education, various secretaries, section chiefs, supervisors, special inspectors, and designated staff members, there were also more than 30 people, including Chen Xunci from the Provincial Library and Hu Chengshu from the Provincial People's Education Center. The opening ceremony was held at 9:00 AM, presided over by Chen Bulei, who delivered the opening remarks. Subsequently, Luo Dixian, Zhang Hangjian, Zhang Rentian, and others delivered speeches. After the opening ceremony, American education expert Luo Ge gave a speech (The Road to Educational Reform in China). After the speech, the first general meeting was held, where Zhao Yuren reported on the results of the designated work of the Provincial Department of Education in the previous session, and Zhao Jiyu reported on the social education institutions of various provinces and the social education substitute institutions in various school districts, as well as the results of the designated work in the previous session. In the afternoon at 2:00 PM, Liang Yihao gave a speech (The Supervision System and the Guiding System). At 3:00 PM, the general meeting continued, discussing the guiding plan for local education in Zhejiang Province in the 21st year and the proposals of various institutions. The meeting continued on the 17th for further discussion, and Cheng Tianfang and Zhao Ting were invited to give speeches.

The Grand Occasion of the Literacy Movement Conference in Zhejiang Province

The Propaganda Committee of the Provincial and Municipal Literacy Movement of Zhejiang Province held its opening ceremony at the Hubin Public Sports Field at 9:00 AM on the 15th. Present were Yang Mianzhong from the Provincial Government, Chen Yisun from the Provincial Party Department, Qian Jiazhi from the Department of Education, Chen Chunren from the Hangzhou Municipal Government, and more than 50 groups from district offices, schools, and institutions in Hangzhou City. Chairman Yang Mianzhong opened the meeting as usual. First, Yang Mianzhong delivered the opening remarks, followed by Qian Jiazhi reporting on the progress of the literacy movement in the past three years, noting that it is now in its third session and greater attention should be paid to promoting people's schools and literacy stations. The population of Zhejiang Province totals over 20,643,000 people. According to the calculation method of the national education plan for implementing adult supplementary education, the total number of people in Zhejiang Province who should receive education in people's schools is over 9,600,000. With 5,000 people per grade and three grades per school, more than 64,000 schools are needed, requiring the establishment of 697 new schools each year, which will take 13 years to achieve universal access. Subsequently, Chen Yisun and Chen Chengren gave speeches one after another and the meeting adjourned. At 6:30 PM in the evening, Dr. Locke, a professor from Columbia University in the United States, gave a public broadcast speech.

The State of Education in Taicang After the Flood and War

▲Deficit of 70,000 to 80,000 Yuan ▲Temporary Austerity Measures ▲Approved by Meeting The education expenses in Taicang, Jiangsu Province, have become difficult to manage. Last summer, it suffered from floods, and this spring, it was affected by war. The local finances are extremely depleted. For the 20th year, about 30,000 yuan of education funds for the first semester are in arrears and have not been paid. In addition, there are outstanding interest-bearing debts of more than 20,000 yuan to the financial sector. The two items total about 60,000 yuan. If based on this year's budget, more than 80,000 yuan is still needed for various budget items in this semester, totaling more than 140,000 yuan. However, according to the Finance Bureau, only more than 60,000 yuan of overdue education expenses have not been collected, resulting in a shortfall of 70,000 to 80,000 yuan. How to make up for this huge deficit is a major problem at present. On the afternoon of the 11th, the reporter specifically interviewed Mr. Hui Meishan, the Director of the Education Bureau. His remarks are recorded below. According to Director Hui, the county's education expenses are extremely exhausted. Seeking new sources of income is not permitted by the facts. Considering the situation, it is necessary to reduce expenditures. Regarding the organization of this bureau, in accordance with the latest standards issued by the Department (Grading Standards and Expenditure Table for Education Bureaus in Various Counties), austerity will be implemented first. The administrative expenses of this bureau after the austerity will be more than 400 yuan per month, only one-third of the previous administrative expenses. Other schools and social education institutions have been suspended since this semester. All principals and directors will be granted leave without pay in this semester, imitating the example of Baoshan County (the teachers of various schools and the staff of various social education institutions may also follow this example). All school and institution buildings, stationery, and other items will still be entrusted to the personnel on leave to properly manage. Starting from May, the bureau will raise and distribute custodial fees on a monthly basis. If there is an immediate need to open schools due to environmental needs, schools and institutions will be established in accordance with the prescribed standards, realistically and pragmatically. Supplementary funding will be provided from the collection of overdue items in the 21st year, and maintenance fees and business expenses will be taken into account. While implementing austerity, the intention is to actively strive for progress. With this approach, if the overdue education expenses can be fully collected in the near future, the past income and expenses can be offset, and the difficult situation thereafter can gradually improve. He also presented a brief record of the austerity measures decided by the Education Administration Committee on the 9th of this month, as follows: A. Elementary Schools (by school) Monthly Custodial Fee Total Custodial Fees for All Levels Single Grade: 3 yuan 273 Two Grades: 4 yuan 76 Three Grades or More: 5 yuan 45 Total: 394 B. Complete Elementary Schools Name of School Monthly Custodial Fee Name of School Monthly Custodial Fee Shixiao: 16 yuan Xintang: 8 yuan Chengshi: 10 yuan Shaxi: 10 yuan Maoshi: 8 yuan Fuqiao: 10 yuan Shuangfeng: 10 yuan Huangjing: 12 yuan Liuhe: 16 yuan Total: 100 yuan C. Shanghai Education After January 28th (6) Still

▲Schools Maintain Classes | Spirit Rejuvenated

9. Maintaining the Reopening of Schools

With lingering fears gradually suppressed, a sense of responsibility gradually emerged, spurring action. By late February, teachers from various troubled areas converged in Shanghai to discuss maintaining the reopening of schools. Shanghai Law College and Fudan Practical High School relocated to the shores of West Lake to hold classes. The affiliated high school of Jinan University moved to the city of Suzhou and hung up its school sign. In addition to opening classes in the concessions, the university headquarters also established a branch in Guangzhou. Sanmin Elementary School sought refuge in Nanhui. Of the remaining 130-plus schools, those with the means rented alternative premises in the special district, including more than ten schools such as Labor University, China Public School, Central Business College, Provincial Shanghai High School, Liangjiang Women's Physical Education School, China Women's Physical Education School, and Nanyang Commercial College. Those without the means had to temporarily merge with existing schools in the special district. Those with neither the means nor any other options had to temporarily close down. The funding for maintenance varied depending on the history, content, activities, and number of students of each school. The luckiest were the Minli High School near Nanmen and the Nanyang High School near Shihui Bridge. Unlike other schools, these two schools opened early, a week before the outbreak of gunfire in Zhabei. Almost all of their students had paid their fees and packed their belongings to enter the school, reciting the classics and the ABCs with confidence. Schools that opened after January 28th found that students were not always understanding of the painstaking efforts of the administrators, and were hesitant to attend classes, resulting in temporary classrooms that were not as bustling as before, with many schools sparsely populated. However, Jinan, Labor, China Public, Shanghai High, Nanyang Model, Jiaotong University and other schools had a considerable number of students. Although the initial war zone was in Zhabei, the impact extended beyond the city of Shanghai. Even youth middle schools in the special district temporarily served as apartments to accommodate fellow citizens in distress. The Youth Association Middle School, Peide Girls' Elementary School, and Tonghui Elementary School, among others, were converted into refugee shelters or wounded soldier hospitals. Moreover, in areas outside of the French Concession and the South Shanghai District, such as Pengpu, Wusong, Jiangwan, Yinxiang, Yinhang, Zhenru, Caoging, Gaogiao, and Fahua, about 50 municipal schools were affected by the war and found it difficult to maintain operations. Schools in areas without troops stationed or artillery fire also had few students for a time. Therefore, among the schools that historically opened around February 3rd or 4th, and continued without interruption, there were likely only a handful, apart from the Municipal Bide Elementary School in the French Concession and a few schools in rural areas. However, even if schools were forced to delay opening, or temporarily suspend classes, or had few students, they immediately resumed classes whenever the opportunity arose. This indomitable spirit of struggle was truly admirable. With the municipal government's revenue plummeting, the initial period of the war was extremely difficult. The monthly operating expenses of the Municipal Education Bureau, originally stipulated at 102,500 yuan, fell to 20,000 yuan. How could this amount be allocated to more than 200 affiliated institutions? In the midst of countless difficulties, the authorities devised an impossible solution to barely maintain operations. This solution was as follows: 1. All municipal primary and secondary schools, except for single-grade elementary schools, would temporarily postpone opening, and teachers and staff would remain on leave without pay. 2. During the period of postponement, schools would handle matters separately according to the following regulations: A. Secondary Schools: (1) The principal of each school would receive a living allowance of 40 yuan and be responsible for the full custody of the school. (2) Each school should retain one clerk, with a monthly living allowance of 30 yuan. (3) Each school should retain two workers each for Wuben and Jingye, four for Xinlu (including two gardeners), two for Wusong, and two for Yangjing, with a monthly salary of 12 yuan per person. (4) All other teachers and staff would remain on leave without pay. (5) The office expenses for each school would be determined as follows: 10 yuan per month for Wuben and Jingye, and 5 yuan per month for Xinlu, Yangjing, and Wusong. B. Elementary Schools: (1) Principals with an original salary of 40 yuan or more would receive a living allowance of 40 yuan; those with less than 40 yuan would receive their original salary and be responsible for the custody of the school. (2) Schools with 12 or more grades should retain one clerk, with a monthly living allowance of 30 yuan. (3) Each school should retain a certain number of custodians: one for schools with six grades or fewer, two for schools with more than six but fewer than twelve grades, and three for schools with more than twelve grades. The monthly salary would be 12 yuan per person in the South Shanghai and Zhabei districts, and 8 yuan per person in other districts. (4) All other teachers and staff would remain on leave without pay. (5) Single-grade elementary schools, except those in the war zone, would open classes as usual, and their office expenses would be temporarily paid from the school construction fund, set at 5 yuan per month. (6) Schools with two or more classrooms that were not in the war zone could continue to operate as usual if they could use the school construction fund revenue to maintain operations after the bombing of the office of the factory department of the French National Labor University. The school would formulate detailed measures and submit them to the bureau for approval. (7) The office expenses for each school would be 3 yuan per month for schools with six grades or fewer, 4 yuan per month for schools with more than six but fewer than twelve grades, and 5 yuan per month for schools with more than twelve grades. Rent and telephone expenses would be provided separately. Besides the above measures, there were indeed no more appropriate solutions. However, schools relied solely on school construction funds for maintenance, and every school complained bitterly. For example, the Municipal Wanzhu Elementary School had 28 grades, and according to the standard, it should have received 560 yuan in administrative expenses, but now it received a total of 5 yuan, including everything. No wonder the administrators were working harder than ever. They were envious of the teachers at Jiaotong University, the only one, who were not in arrears of their salaries. One People's Education Center: 25 yuan Second People's Education Center: 12 yuan Simple People's Education Center: 10 yuan Arts and Crafts Training Center: 12 yuan Experimental District: 12 yuan Women's Vocational School: 3 yuan Agricultural Education Center: 8 yuan Tea Garden Night School, etc.: temporarily suspended Total: 82 yuan E. Expansion of Soochow Law School

The curriculum and organization of the Law School of Soochow University have always been divided into two parts: the university law preparatory course and the undergraduate course. It is heard that starting from the next academic year, the preparatory and undergraduate courses will be merged, and the university will adopt a five-year graduation system. High school graduates can apply for the first grade of the law department. Students who have completed one year of university studies can apply for the second grade. Students who have completed two or more years of university studies, and graduates of non-law departments from domestic and foreign universities, can apply for the third grade. Graduates of domestic and foreign university law departments who have obtained a law degree can apply for the graduate school. Due to the current situation, the school address has been temporarily moved from Kunshan Road to 103 Seymour Road. A two-cent stamp must be attached to requests for prospectuses. National Jinan University

Organizing the Post-War Restoration Committee

▲Approved Guiding Principles ▲Established Divisional Responsibilities As the Japanese army is about to withdraw from Zhenru, Jinan University believes that its school buildings will soon be recovered and that timely restoration work is urgently needed. It has organized a Post-War Restoration Committee and held its first meeting yesterday. The meeting resolved to approve the committee's guiding principles and several important cases. The following is a special recording for reference by other schools in the war zone for receiving and restoring their facilities. (First Meeting of the Restoration Committee) The meeting was held on May 16th. Attendees: Sun Hanbing, Fan Shouzhi, Zheng Baoning, Chen Kemei, Xu Kecheng, Xi Yushu, Yang Yufen, Ye Yuan, Yu Jitai, Lin Zhiying, Yang Yufen (proxy). Chairman: Chen Kemei. Recorder: Yang Yufen. After the opening ceremony, (1) A draft of the committee's guiding principles was proposed for public decision. Resolution: Amended and approved. (2) A resolution was proposed to determine the date of the committee's regular meetings. Resolution: Regular meetings will be held every other Thursday at 4:00 PM. (3) A resolution was proposed to organize the committee members in accordance with Article 2 of the committee's guiding principles. Resolution: Group A: School Affairs Group: Chen Kemei, Zhang Feng, Yu Jitai, Sun Hanbing, Ye Yuan, Fan Shouzhi, Yang Yufen, Zheng Baoning, Xi Yushu. Convened by Chen Kemei. Group B: School Property Group: Yu Jitai, Ye Yuan, Xi Yushu, Chen Zhiying, Xu Kecheng. Convened by Yu Jitai. Group C: School Building Group: Fan Shouzhi, Sun Hanbing, Zheng Baoning, Lin Zhiying, Xu Kecheng. Convened by Fan Shouzhi. Group D: General Affairs Group: Yang Yufen, Zhang Feng, Chen Kemei. Convened by Yang Yufen. (4) A resolution was proposed to determine the meeting times for each group. Resolution: The School Affairs Group will meet every Friday at 4:00 PM. The meeting times for the remaining groups will be determined by themselves. (Guiding Principles of the Post-War Restoration Committee) (1) The name of the committee is the National Jinan University Post-War Restoration Committee. (2) The tasks of the committee are listed on the left: A. School Affairs: To draft the number of faculty and staff positions and the allocation of duties, revise the curriculum, design moral education, and determine the number of students. B. School Property: To measure and inspect school property, compile lists of buildings, land, books, instruments, school equipment, etc. C. School Buildings: To repair or renovate school buildings, allocate classrooms, offices, and dormitories. D. General Affairs: To handle matters not covered by the above items. (3) The committee will consist of 11 to 15 members, all appointed by the president. (4) The committee will establish an office on the Shanghai campus. (5) The committee will appoint a number of staff members, assigned by the school. (6) The committee's funding is tentatively set at 1,000 yuan, to be paid by the finance office at any time. (7) If the committee encounters special matters that require the assistance of experts from outside the school, the expenses will be approved by the president and paid by the finance office. (8) The committee will meet once every two weeks. The date and time will be determined by the first meeting. Special meetings will be convened when necessary. (9) A quorum for committee meetings is more than half of the members. All motions must be approved by more than two-thirds of the members present. (10) Matters not covered in these guiding principles may be amended at any time with the approval of the committee. (11) These guiding principles will be implemented from the date of promulgation by the president after being approved by a special school affairs meeting.

A Letter to People Interested in Education and Forestry in Jiangsu (1)

Li Yingong respectfully submits this letter. Yingong has been in charge of the Jiangsu Provincial Education Forest from April of the 17th year of the Republic to February of the 21st year, a period of less than four years. Although I have worked diligently in the public interest, I am afraid that there are still areas where I have not been able to meet people's expectations. I would like to briefly explain this. Initially, the forest area was repeatedly ravaged by bandits, and the buildings and gardens were in a state of widespread dilapidation. The forests were also in a similar condition. Anyone involved in the matter could speak to this. After I took over, I carefully formulated annual plans, revised the methods, and strived to improve efficiency in business. Therefore, I did not hesitate to use all the funds (at that time, the annual fee was 30,800 yuan, which was later increased to 32,000 yuan), with nine-tenths used for the forest area business, and one-tenth allocated for necessary administrative and miscellaneous expenses. This is detailed in the past annual reports, so there is no need to list them all. Generally, people in Jiangsu feel that education funds are scarce and are ignorant of forest management principles. There are occasionally criticisms that are too demanding and far removed from the facts. Yingong has never taken offense. However, it is not convincing for people in the education field to echo these sentiments (I recall that last year, a certain person copied a friend's outdated and decaying newspaper from the previous year and used it to stir up trouble and incite a revolt to sell his disruptive skills). I want to be able to explain myself, but how can I? I will discuss the points of misunderstanding below. (1) Pruning pine trees, according to planting statistics, the cost should yield huge profits (Answer) This is too idealistic. After trees are densely planted, side branches have few opportunities to flourish. How is it different for young pine trees? Pruning pine trees is not a necessary procedure in nurturing them. Even if pruning is advocated, it should not be done for trees under ten years of age. Moreover, if the pruning is not done properly, it can easily leave dead knots, which will directly reach the heartwood, causing unlimited losses. The reason why the education forest occasionally prunes is to cut down lower branches to isolate weeds to help prevent fires, and to use the branches to accumulate and sell, which can help increase income. The amount of pruning per year follows established precedents, and the forest area, which was established early on, supervises the forest workers to select for pruning, or adopts the method of branch division by rural farmers. The area is about 2,000 mu per year, in order to produce good timber from those pruned. Beyond this, there is no need for pruning. Those that are too overgrown will be thinned. However, the trees planted in the earliest period of the education forest have not yet reached the age of thinning (The age of ordinary forest trees reaches about 20 years before thinning is considered). The education forest was only established in the fifth year of the Republic, and the trees in the first forest area are still under 15 or 16 years old, not to mention others. As for pruning miscellaneous trees, it is not always necessary, or for natural forests, once every five or seven years, then it belongs to the reorganization work to promote growth and is not concerned with profit.

Gold Price Plummets

▲Decline Reaches Seventeen Taels ▲Impacted by the Death of the Japanese Prime Minister

The gold exchange reopened yesterday, though hit hard by the news of the Japanese Prime Minister's passing. Gold prices dropped sharply, though the morning and afternoon markets did not change much. The difference between the initial and final prices was fourteen taels, with the total drop reaching seventeen taels. It initially plummeted twenty taels, then broke through 690 taels. This was largely due to the assassination and subsequent death of Japanese Prime Minister Inukai Tsuyoshi, leading to fears of a worsening world situation. The rise in silver prices further fueled panic. As foreign exchange rates shifted from deficit to equilibrium, those covering their positions in the industry entered the market, causing the gold price to rebound by ten taels. The afternoon market initially returned to 700 taels but later weakened. Exchange rates appeared to strengthen. The day's situation is recorded below:

▲Opening Plunge of Twenty-Four and a Half Taels

The seven-month contract opened at 690.5 taels, a plunge of 24.5 taels. Large bars of silver rose by 16/1, with the price of silver rising a total of 7/8 in two days, and private telegrams adding 3/4. It then rebounded by three taels to 93.5 taels due to successful purchases by Yuanheng, Wanxing, and Shunli. Soon after, Fuyu, Dadecheng, Hongkang, Yongyuan, and Dayong all sold, exacerbated by a weakening US dollar. The August initial price of 32.5 yuan plummeted by six taels to 87.5 taels. Hengyu, Hengxing, Fuyu, Shunli, and Neixing bought in, and HSBC absorbed half a yuan of August US dollars, reaching 95.5 taels at 9:30 AM. British gold was up half a penny, and the US dollar at 75, retreated to 93 taels. Afterwards, Fuyu, Zhifeng, Yongyi, Fengyong, Hengxing, Tongchun, Yuanheng, Xiehing, and Yong competed to buy again. US dollars for June at 75 and September at 32.25 were eagerly purchased by banks. At 10:15 AM, it reached 99 taels, fluctuating by only one or two taels. Then, Longsheng, Yuanda, Yongyuan, Taitai, Tongtaichang, Fuchang, Yifeng, and Yong came to sell, and it immediately depreciated by five taels. After 10:30 AM, it was at 94 taels, then rebounded by five taels, fluctuating by only two taels. The Dalian gang and Yifeng, Yongyuan, Chengyong, and Hengyu bought in, and the US dollar also stabilized. HSBC absorbed 1.875, and the Belgian Bank absorbed 0.0625 for August. Then, the Japanese Bank bought 32 yuan. Until 11:30 AM, it was at 99 taels and three qian. Then, goods hedging and small retail longs came to sell, and it immediately shaved off two taels. At 11:40 AM, it was at 97 taels, and remained flat thereafter. The noon closing price was 97 taels and seven qian, with the listed price changed to 768 taels, with a squeeze of 72.3 taels. The noon closing price was 70 taels.

▲Afternoon Market Continues to Decline

The afternoon market opened at 701 taels, then 701.5 taels. The Dalian gang and Hengyu initially bought actively. Later, Zhifeng, Yonghong, and Kangyong sold. The August US dollar initially absorbed 32 yuan, then sold at the same price. Pan Gen bought 0.25 for September, so the gold price fell by four or five taels to 696 taels and eight qian at 2:20 PM. Later, Yuanmao, Yongheng, Hengyu, Dadecheng, and Yifengyong competed to buy, and September US dollars could be sold at 1.25, causing morale to rise, reaching 700 taels and three qian around 3:00 PM. Suddenly, small amounts appeared, fluctuating by two taels. At 4:00 PM, Zhifengyong, Qianchangxiang, and Chengyongyong had strong selling pressure, and September US dollars were trading at 1.25, causing the gold price to plunge by four taels to 96 taels and two qian at 4:10 PM. At the 4:30 PM closing, it was 98 taels, a sharp drop of seventeen taels compared to last Saturday (the first day of the swap). The maximum price for the day was 701.5 taels, and the minimum was 687.5 taels, a difference of fourteen taels. The listed price squeezed between 67.8 taels and 72 taels, then 70 taels. The book prices for May and June were both 701 taels, July was 698 taels, the replenishment was 701 taels, and the naked bar added 9.5 taels.

▲Extraordinary Public Panic

Statistical Summary of Table Transactions

Yuanheng, Yifengyong, Shunli, Wanxing, Hengxing, Hengyu, Qianchangxiang, Tongchun, Futaiheng, Yuanguangxiang, and Tongchang all bought in, as did a certain firm on behalf of Yufengyong, covering exchange drafts. Government Bonds Suddenly Drop by About One Yuan

▲Trading Volume Exceeds 2.8 Million Yuan

Yesterday (the 17th), various bond market conditions in the Chinese Securities Exchange. Although several spot markets opened, except for approximately 10,000 for '96' and 'Entire 6', the rest were only several thousand yuan, totaling 32,000 yuan. In the futures market, price fluctuations were significant, and buying and selling activity was quite lively, making market conditions far better than before. The morning saw 1.28 million yuan, and the afternoon saw over 1.5 million yuan, totaling 2,855,000 yuan. Among these, unified salt tax bonds of 20 volumes each accounted for 47-480,000 yuan, while others also totaled over 300,000 yuan. However, '96', customs duties, and retrenchment were very quiet. As for the trend of various bond prices, in the early morning, the market showed no changes, and prices continued to hover. Fluctuations were very slight compared to the previous day. Suddenly, market sentiment weakened, and selling transactions were particularly active. Although buyers were not inactive, the situation of supply exceeding demand was very obvious. Consequently, prices of various bonds fell sharply in unison, dropping about one yuan more than in the morning, and each fell by a little 0.7-0.8 jiao to one yuan or more compared to the previous day. Only financial prices remained slightly firm. The reason for the price drop was that changes in the Japanese political situation and the future of Sino-Japanese diplomacy were generally predicted to be unfavorable.

New York Stock Market Shows Slight Rebound

(Report from American Eastern Bank)

Yesterday, Monday, the New York Stock Market opened with quotes lower than those of Saturday. Later, news of rising wheat prices buoyed sentiment, and seasoned traders seized the opportunity to buy. As the market neared closing, short positions were covered, further improving the atmosphere. The closing price was generally higher than the previous day, with industrial stocks averaging a gain of 1.48 pounds. The main concerns in yesterday's market were the sharp falls in the Japanese yen and government bonds. Cotton piece goods prices also fell, but because the rise in wheat prices was a stronger influence, it had no impact. However, yesterday's price improvements should not be considered stable, as there are still many negative factors. For example, the dividend reduction of the "DuPont de Nemours" company to one dollar is more than enough to offset the rise in wheat prices. Although everyone is hoping for continued and greater improvements, unless there is good economic news, it is uncertain whether yesterday's prices can hold.

Yarn and Cotton Markets Sluggish

The cotton yarn market is again in a stagnant state, with an extremely loose situation. This is because, after extreme activity, there must naturally be a period of rest. Therefore, there is less demand from various yarn groups, resulting in demoralization. However, the situation of various factories is better. So, realistically speaking, the price of 154-155 taels for standard yarn should be sustainable. However, those outside the industry see business as not improving and are still cautious, and new entrants have not yet enthusiastically entered the market, so the market atmosphere is wavering. However, in this unfavorable surrounding environment, the power to rise is very difficult. The current situation still does not escape the realm of hovering.

Previous Week's American Cotton

Gradually Entering a State of Chaos

A New York telegram from May 13 reported on the cotton market situation for the week: Raw cotton buying has gradually decreased this week. The price increases of last week have lost some of their buying momentum due to scattered selling and liquidation. Due to disappointing securities market conditions, reports of smooth progress in Southern cotton crops, and the uncertainty of various bills in Congress, Southern spot conditions have not eased. It is heard that demand is sluggish and there are not many sellers. Traders have stopped May deliveries, and it is rumored that about 20,000 bales of cotton for New York May delivery will be shipped to Germany and Liverpool. Temperatures are still causing concern in many places, as dry weather is currently conducive to cotton crop development. At the same time, there is still bullish sentiment, based on the fact that prices are already low and a bumper cotton harvest may not be possible. This sentiment can be seen in the slight buying when market prices fall.

Silk and Tea Markets - Tea Market Downtrend Unabated

Yesterday, in the foreign merchant tea market in this port, both road tea and local tea, the Zhenmei green tea from firms such as Yingzhuang, Xiehe, Jinlong, and Tongfu, all had sporadic purchases, but because the incoming prices from abroad were too low, and the exchange rate continued to be high, the recognized prices were even more stringent than before. The city-wide transactions of Zhenmei and Zhenmei needle tea totaled over 460 cases, and the selling price fell again by two to three taels compared to the previous day. As for Qimen, Fuliang, and Jiande road black tea, 11,754 cases have already arrived. After two days of lengthy negotiations between Chinese and foreign parties, new prices have still not been announced, and the situation is quite pessimistic.

Yushan Green Tea Opens at High Price

The Yushan and Shangrao areas of Jiangxi Province have always been known for their abundant tea production. Recently, large quantities of new goods have been launched on the market in places such as Zhengjiafang and Zhangcunjie. Foreign firms, due to making significant profits last year, continue to work tirelessly despite the frequent alarms of banditry. According to news from that area, the Zhengjiafang first-grade spring tea has already opened, with a price of 52 yuan per dan, which is 15-16 yuan higher than last year. However, it is said to be tender, and the quality seems better than in previous years.

Grain and Rice Markets Uniformly Tighten

▲Yesterday, the west road in northern Shanghai had more than 10 sources, but the store appetite in this city was not smooth. The buy-in of shadowed yuan was quite vigorous, and the large plate suddenly rose by 0.1-0.2 yuan.

The Trend of Head Cloths and Piece Goods is Dull

The piece goods market has been particularly dull in recent days. Local customers have shown no excitement. The reasons for this are: first, the end of May is approaching, and funds are tight, so people are hesitant to purchase more; second, Eastern goods are very active, and their quoted prices are lower than domestic goods, so that most of the sales channels of the shops on this street have been seized by them; and third, it is the off-season, coupled with the fact that the Yangtze River area has not yet recovered from the floods and is also affected by the rampant Communist bandits, which makes it difficult to make progress. Yesterday, the prices of domestic cotton cloth still fell more than they rose. Thirteen-pound cloth remained stable at 5 liang and 4 qian. Eleven-pound cloth fell to 4 liang and 7 qian. Local customers were more active in fine cloth, but were constrained by Japanese factory goods, and prices fell step by step. Twelve-pound cloth is on the verge of falling to 7 liang. However, the price decline of 13-pound Hubei goods has slowed down recently due to purchases from Yantai, Qingdao, and other gangs. Yesterday, Wannianging was sold for 8 liang and 5 qian, Saima for 8 liang and 3 qian. Western goods were mostly sold in small quantities. Striped poplin moved slightly more than before, with those priced around 3 qian being the most popular. White striped linen and ramie cloth are still being purchased by Ningbo and other ports on this street, and prices are neither high nor low.
